# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Django Migration Squash and Dependency Compliance

## Your Task

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

Perfect! I've successfully created the `/workspace/answer.json` file with a comprehensive analysis of Django's migration squashing compliance implementation. 

The answer includes:

1. **9 Key Python Source Files** implementing migration squashing:
   - squashmigrations.py - The main command generator
   - migration.py - Migration class with replaces attribute
   - graph.py - Migration dependency graph handling
   - loader.py - Loading and managing replaced migrations
   - executor.py - Applying migrations with replacement tracking
   - writer.py - Serializing migrations with replaces attribute
   - recorder.py - Recording migration application status
   - migrate.py - Validating squash completeness
   - exceptions.py - Migration-related exceptions

2. **7 Core Symbol Classes** representing the main components of the squashing system

3. **7-Function Execution Chain** showing how squash migrations flow through the system

4. **Detailed Narrative Explanation** describing:
   - How the squash migration generator creates new migrations with the `replaces` attribute
   - How replaced-migrations are tracked across the system
   - How the dependency graph validates that replaced nodes are properly remapped
   - How the squash completeness check ensures consistency between disk and database state

The implementation ensures that Django can safely squash migrations while maintaining complete backward compatibility and tracking which migrations have been replaced.

MigrationGraph.validate_consistency() (lines 198-200) ensures no dummy nodes remain in the graph\\n   - MigrationLoader.replace_migration() (lines 235-272 in loader.py) handles the replacement logic, checking if replaced migrations are all applied/unapplied and managing the graph accordingly\\n   - MigrationLoader._resolve_replaced_migration_keys() (lines 224-233) recursively resolves all replaced migration keys, handling cases where replaced migrations are themselves replaced\\n   - MigrationLoader.build_graph() (lines 274-342) orchestrates the entire graph building process with validation\\n   - MigrationLoader.check_consistent_history() (lines 344-370) validates that applied migrations don't have unapplied dependencies, with special handling for squashed migrations\\n\\n4. **Squash Completeness Check** (django/db/migrations/executor.py and django/core/management/commands/migrate.py):\\n   - MigrationLoader.all_replaced_applied() (lines 372-384 in loader.py) recursively checks whether all replaced migrations are applied\\n   - MigrationExecutor.record_migration() (lines 268-277 in executor.py) records the application status of migrations, with special handling for replacement migrations - it recursively records the status of all replaced migrations\\n   - MigrationExecutor.check_replacements() (lines 294-308 in executor.py) marks replacement migrations as applied if all their replaced migrations are applied, even if the replacement migration didn't apply anything new itself\\n   - The migrate command (lines 202-224 in django/core/management/commands/migrate.py) validates squash completeness by checking that squashed migrations with deleted replaced migrations cannot be pruned, and provides user feedback about the need to run migrate to properly record the applied state\\n   - MigrationRecorder.record_applied() and record_unapplied() (lines 99-107 in recorder.py) handle the actual database recording of migration application status\\n\\nThe flow works as follows: When squashmigrations command creates a new migration, MigrationWriter generates the migration file with the 'replaces' list. When the migrations are loaded via MigrationLoader.build_graph(), the loader identifies all replacing migrations and calls replace_migration() for each one. This method resolves all replaced migration keys (handling nested squashing), checks their applied status, and either removes the replaced nodes from the graph (if all are applied/unapplied) or removes the replacement node (if partially applied). Finally, MigrationExecutor.check_replacements() ensures that the replacement migration is marked as applied in the database if all its replaced migrations are applied, maintaining consistency even when migrations are pushed to deployments where the replaced migrations are already applied.\"\n}\n",
